# TypeSharp Language And Adoption 1.0 Progress

Last updated: 2026-05-26

This file tracks implementation progress for [lang-1.0-tasks.md](lang-1.0-tasks.md). It is a manual progress ledger, not a task queue.

## Status Legend

| Status | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| Not started | No current implementation evidence. |
| In progress | Work has started, but required evidence is incomplete. |
| Blocked by decision | A policy/design decision is required before implementation can continue. |
| Blocked by release infrastructure | Requires packaging, signing, hosting, or release artifact infrastructure. |
| Evidence needed | Implementation likely exists, but 1.0-level proof is missing or too narrow. |
| Done | The item has direct evidence covering the stated 1.0 requirement. |
| Deferred | Explicitly moved to post-1.0 or non-goal. |

## Current Focus

| Field | Value |
| --- | --- |
| Current slice | First hosted release/download smoke is green on `v0.1.0-preview.4`, and the first-project plus webpage-to-build adoption route is closed; remaining pre-1.0 work is broader MVP-limited language parity, not the release/install path. |
| Primary source | [lang-1.0-tasks.md](lang-1.0-tasks.md) |
| Verification target | Test catalog tracker-count guard, workflow contract, diagnostic fixture README drift checks, docs contract, compiler test build, docs build, diff hygiene, workflow/docs-script forbidden-tooling scan, deployed public-docs probe, and hosted-release probe. |
| External evidence state | GitHub Pages API reports workflow deployment at `https://naramdash.github.io/TypeSharp/`. The `be320542569bf50cb295acc012fb81d699a007ee` release push proved Docs run `26394300733`, Regression run `26394300735`, release-dispatched Docs run `26394397996`, and Release Artifacts run `26394303889` all succeed. The later `40f7be4990920b0d3d6c423142d8324f42eb47dd` tracker-evidence push proved Docs run `26396589064` and Regression run `26396589100` both succeed after the hosted-release tracker reconciliation. `v0.1.0-preview.4` is published at `https://github.com/naramdash/TypeSharp/releases/tag/v0.1.0-preview.4` with uploaded CLI, runtime, VSIX, and `SHA256SUMS.txt` assets, and the hosted release smoke passed download, API digest, checksum, version, clean project, dependency, generated-build-failure, project-reference, runtime library, and C# `net48` consumer checks. |
| Last verification | 2026-05-26 generated record member public ABI snapshot evidence: `dotnet build test\TypeSharp.Compiler.Tests\TypeSharp.Compiler.Tests.csproj`, targeted generated immutable record public ABI smoke, docs-site contract, test-runner shard, docs build, rendered install-route verifier, diff hygiene, and stale record ABI wording scan passed locally. | Resume note | Broad `TS2201` checker dispatch is closed, and `v0.1.0-preview.4` provides the first hosted release/download smoke evidence. Reopen adoption-route work only if release artifacts, starter templates, public docs, or hosted smoke coverage change. |

| Publish official CLI download/install path | Done | README and docs now link to an Install page that defines GitHub Release asset names, release notes, checksum verification for CLI and runtime archives, the current checksum-only preview signature policy, extraction, `typesharp.cmd`, `PATH`, `typesharp version`, runtime zip, uninstall steps, and direct rollback steps for a previous CLI/runtime archive pair. Docs contract coverage now asserts the rollback section verifies both the previous CLI archive and previous runtime archive before extracting the CLI and running `typesharp.cmd version`. Docs contract coverage also preserves the `typesharp version` target split in Install (`Target default net48`, `CLI target net10.0`, `Runtime target net48`) and the Troubleshooting warning not to retarget generated `net48` projects to satisfy CLI host prerequisites. The docs primary Learn sidebar now exposes Install before Start Here, and the docs home first link list puts the release Install path before Start Here; docs contract coverage preserves both orderings, and the GitHub Pages workflow now repeats that check against rendered sidebar links plus the docs-home next-page pagination link before uploading the Pages artifact. | Ship and resolve Core/Runtime dependencies | Done | Runtime Artifacts and Install document the 1.0 runtime resolution policy: download the matching `typesharp-runtime-net48-<tag>.zip` archive, verify it against `SHA256SUMS.txt`, extract it to `$runtimeRoot`, and reference `lib/net48/TypeSharp.Core.dll` plus `lib/net48/TypeSharp.Runtime.dll` through explicit local `references.paths`. Docs contract coverage preserves the runtime archive expansion command and `$runtimeRoot` reference wording. The release-staged runtime helper now packages the Core/Runtime layout into `typesharp-runtime-net48-staged-test.zip`, adds and verifies a lowercase SHA-256 manifest entry in the same staged `SHA256SUMS.txt`, extracts the archive, verifies the runtime README tag/build/source/ABI/target metadata plus `lib/net48` DLL list, then builds a TypeSharp library from a clean workspace using those extracted DLL paths and compiles a separate C# `net48` consumer against the generated assembly plus installed Core/Runtime DLLs while calling `TypeSharpUnion` and `TypeSharpAsync` helper APIs. API and user docs now state that direct TypeSharp source imports named `Some`/`None`/`Ok`/`Error` are future ergonomics, while the current Core ABI exposes C# static factories such as `Result<T,E>.Ok(...)`. | Reopen only if CLI auto-copy, hidden template references, or a different runtime acquisition path is promoted into 1.0. |

Staged generated C# build-failure smoke reports `TS3501` after successful `check`, and now verifies JSON `TS3501` keeps error severity and the generated project name. Docs contract tests assert the generated-project-relative `HintPath` and offline `NuGet.config` policy stays documented. | Reopen only if dependency behavior changes or package restore is promoted. |

Staged artifact library dependency plus C# consumer smoke passes through the same wrapper. ## Language Progress

| Item | Status | Current evidence | Next action |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Imported C# mutable-local checked/unchecked user-defined multiplicative operator policy | Done | The metadata reader/type checker policy is now recorded as ordinary C# public static binary `op_Multiply`, `op_Division`, and `op_Modulus` only. Checked user-defined operator metadata names `op_CheckedMultiply`, `op_CheckedDivision`, and `op_CheckedModulus` are documented as post-1.0 and rejected with deterministic `TS2217` when no ordinary operator is available. Focused checker coverage now exercises checked-only multiply, division, and modulus metadata; the existing generated `net48` consumer smoke preserves accepted checked/unchecked wrapper lowering around ordinary compound assignments. Docs contract assertions keep the Type System and .NET Interop wording present. | Reopen only if generated output moves beyond the C# 7.3 compatibility target or true checked user-defined operators are promoted into 1.0. |
| Public ABI language matrix | Done | `docs/src/content/docs/csharp-type-model.md` now has a public declaration ABI matrix covering `fun`, `record`, `class`, `interface`, `delegate`, `event`, `enum`, `union`, `type` aliases, extension methods, and getter-only extension properties. It marks promoted public ABI slices separately from compile-time-only and deferred forms. TypeSharp-authored `fun` public ABI lowering preserves static method metadata for explicit parameters, `params`, optional/default, generic constraints, and generic optional/default parameter subsets with backend/generated source checks, generated `net48` metadata snapshots, and C# consumer evidence. TypeSharp-authored `record`, `union`, and `delegate` public ABI lowering preserves declaration attributes on generated CLR-visible types, record snapshots now assert constructor/property/equality members, and TypeSharp-authored enum public ABI lowering preserves declaration/member attributes on generated CLR enum metadata, with backend snapshots, generated `net48` build evidence, and C# consumer evidence; TypeSharp-authored class/interface `event` public ABI lowering is promoted for typed events backed by named delegates, including class static events, backend snapshots, generated public ABI snapshots, and generated `net48` C# consumer subscription evidence. Generated public ABI snapshots now preserve type and method generic parameter constraints for generated generic functions, classes, interfaces, and delegates, with direct interface and delegate type-constraint snapshot evidence. Docs contract tests assert the matrix and remaining event backlog wording stay present. | Reopen only if TypeSharp-authored custom add/remove event lowering, interface static event lowering, delegate overload ranking, delegate variance annotations, nested delegates, alternate union representations, arbitrary computed enum values, broader enum attribute target validation, function overload ranking, broader higher-order function inference, or generated event invocation helpers are promoted into 1.0. |
| TypeSharp-authored class/interface/member semantics | Done | Type System now has a named 1.0 Class Interface And Member Boundary. The accepted class surface lowers to named CLR classes with optional type parameters, supported C# 7.3-compatible generic constraints, declaration attributes, `partial`, an implicit public parameterless constructor when no parameter list is declared, an explicit constructor parameter list with CLR-visible parameter types, public instance/static `fun` methods, typed instance/static `let` and `let mut` values, typed instance/static getter-only properties with explicit initializers, typed instance/static mutable get/set auto-properties with explicit initializers, typed instance/static `event` members backed by named delegates, and supported member attributes on emitted methods, values, properties, and events. The accepted interface surface lowers to named CLR interfaces with optional type parameters, supported generic constraints, declaration attributes, `partial`, method signatures, typed instance getter-only properties, typed instance mutable get/set properties, typed instance `event` members backed by named delegates, and supported member attributes on emitted methods, properties, and events. The checker now reports deterministic `TS2210` diagnostics for TypeSharp-authored class constructor parameters missing explicit CLR-visible types, constructor `params` parameter shape failures, class getter-only or mutable get/set properties missing explicit CLR-visible types or initializers, class property setter shapes outside mutable get/set auto-properties, custom accessor shapes, interface getter-only or mutable get/set properties missing explicit CLR-visible types or using initializers/custom accessor shapes, immutable interface property setter shapes, class/interface events without an explicit delegate type, class values missing explicit CLR-visible types or initializers, interface fields, and unsupported skipped class/interface member syntax before backend emission. TypeSharp-authored constructor bodies, constructor parameter capture, constructor default parameters, explicit inheritance/implementation clauses, static member forms beyond class static methods/values/events/properties, abstract/virtual/override members, interface default implementations, custom property accessors, indexers, operators, accessor/parameter attributes, partial methods, nested type declarations, custom add/remove events, interface static events, generated event invocation helpers, broader attribute target validation, and broader member-body analysis remain post-1.0. Generated public ABI snapshots now include generic type and method constraints, constructors, static/instance method modifiers, readonly/static fields, getter/setter property shape, and event add/remove/static shape for generated class/interface members, and generated `net48` C# consumer smokes cover class APIs, class declaration attributes, class member attributes, class explicit constructor calls, class instance/static method calls, class instance/static value reads/writes, class instance/static getter-only property reads, class instance/static get/set property reads/writes, class instance/static event subscription metadata, interface APIs, interface declaration attributes, interface member attributes, interface getter-only property reads, interface get/set property reads/writes, interface event subscription metadata, generic classes, generic constraints, and partial module/record/union/class/interface declarations; build-stop coverage verifies unsupported member forms emit no generated C# source/project/assembly. | Reopen only if TypeSharp-authored constructor bodies, constructor parameter capture/defaults, custom property accessors, custom add/remove events, interface static events, inheritance/implementation clauses, static member forms beyond class static methods/values/events/properties, abstract/virtual/override members, interface default implementations, indexers, operators, accessor/parameter attributes, partial methods, nested types, generated event invocation helpers, broader attribute target validation, or broader member-body analysis are promoted into 1.0. |
| Public ABI leakage checks | Done | Public-boundary diagnostics now cover exported/public function parameters and returns, public delegate parameters and returns, exported/public values, local export-list functions, local export-list type aliases, direct aliases, aliases to structural shapes, intersections, type-level unions, `keyof`, indexed access, inline anonymous structural shapes, and `unknown` public signatures. Build-stop coverage verifies `TS2204` prevents generated source/project/assembly emission. Marker-free `dynamic` is covered by capability diagnostics (`TS2206`/`TS2207`), unknown access by `TS2209`, and unknown C# nullability by strict-mode `TS2404` warnings. Docs contract asserts the public ABI leakage boundary stays documented in Type System, C# And CLR Type Model, and .NET Interop. | Reopen only if a nominal structural public ABI adapter or public `unknown`/computed-type policy is promoted. |
| Module graph boundary | Done | Modules And Imports now records the 1.0 source graph boundary: source imports resolve only through relative specifiers, current-project manifest aliases, or direct TypeSharp project references; non-relative specifiers without a direct project-reference match are C# namespace/type imports; side-effect-only imports report `TS0113`; missing source exports report `TS0114`; non-relative forwarding, cross-project forwarding, and non-lowerable forwarding report `TS2003`; direct project references expose source-level exports only to direct dependents and do not grant hidden transitive visibility. Focused tests cover unresolved source modules plus side-effect-only imports, project-reference source imports and build order, project-reference re-export rejection, unsupported export forwarding build-stop behavior, relative star re-export lowering, and source-alias re-export lowering. | Reopen only if package-style resolution, side-effect imports, cross-project forwarding, hidden transitive visibility, or source navigation promises are promoted into 1.0. |
| Pattern matching boundary | Done | Type System, Feature Status, and Grammar now define the 1.0 executable match boundary: nominal union case names with optional single identifier payload capture, TypeSharp-owned and named imported C# enum member names, `true`/`false`, literal-only local type-level union members, typed member patterns for non-literal local type-level unions, `_`, and `when` guard type checks. Exhaustiveness covers nominal unions, TypeSharp-owned enums, named imported C# enums, `bool`, non-literal local type-level unions, and literal-only local type-level unions; guarded arms do not prove coverage. Unsupported record/structural patterns, nested payload destructuring, extractor-style patterns, standalone identifier binding patterns, ordinary numeric patterns, numeric enum patterns, and flag-style enum/pattern algebra now report `TS2211` or remain documented parser-only backlog before emission. Focused tests cover unsupported-pattern diagnostics, imported enum exhaustiveness, enum match lowering, type-level union narrowing lowering, type-checker fixture diagnostics, and docs contract assertions. | Reopen only if record/structural patterns, nested destructuring, extractors, numeric pattern algebra, flag-style enum reasoning, or broader guard analysis are promoted into 1.0. |
| Advanced type operator limits | Done | Type System, Feature Status, and Diagnostics now define the 1.0 executable type-operator subset: local type-level union aliases, structural intersection aliases over named shapes, limited `keyof` over known records/shapes, and limited indexed access over known records/shapes and literal key unions. The checker now reports `TS2212` for type alias chains deeper than 16, recursive alias cycles, local union aliases wider than 64 distinct members, `keyof`/indexed access aliases with more than 64 selected keys, and structural intersection aliases with more than 64 resulting members. General mapped, conditional, template-literal, and utility type computation remains post-1.0. Public-boundary `TS2204` coverage remains the guard for type-level unions, structural shapes, intersections, `keyof`, indexed access, and unresolved computed forms. Focused tests cover budget diagnostics, existing type-checker fixtures cover positive/negative limited operators, backend fixtures cover lowering for private/internal `keyof` and indexed access aliases, and docs contract asserts the boundary. | Reopen only if mapped/conditional/template/utility evaluator syntax, broader generic type operators, structural public ABI adapters, or larger budgets are promoted into 1.0. |
| C# overload and conversion ranking | Done | C# Members And Overloads now freezes the 1.0 overload and conversion ranking matrix: arity, named arguments, optional parameters, `params`, byref modifiers, exact nominal matches, `null`, numeric literals, metadata relationship distance, homogeneous collection expressions, delegates/lambdas, generic methods/constructors and constraints, imported extension receivers, indexers, nullable metadata checks, and `object` fallback. Feature Status summarizes the same contract and keeps full C# overload conversion parity, user-defined conversion operators, TypeSharp-authored operator overload ranking, richer contextual typing, imported pipeline/composition overload ranking, general collection-builder conversions, function-typed value overload inference, and dynamic dispatch without capability boundaries post-1.0. Existing generated `net48` and build-stop smokes cover exact overloads, object fallback, `null`, metadata relationships, collection expression overloads, numeric literal conversions, named/optional/`params`/byref calls, delegate/lambda return ranking, imported extension receiver ranking, generic constraints, constructor/indexer overloads, `TS2406` no-match, `TS2402` ambiguity, and `TS2417` generic constraint failures. Docs contract assertions preserve the matrix. | Reopen only if full C# overload conversion parity, user-defined conversions, TypeSharp-authored operator overload ranking, richer contextual typing, imported pipeline/composition overload ranking, general collection-builder conversions, function-typed value overload inference, or dynamic dispatch without capability boundaries are promoted into 1.0. |
| Nullability and `unknown` rules | Done | Type System now has a named 1.0 Nullability And Unknown Boundary, and C# And CLR Type Model plus Feature Status summarize the same warning-versus-error policy. TypeSharp-owned nullable-to-non-null flow reports error `TS2202`; public `unknown` and other compile-time-only public boundaries report error `TS2204`; member/indexer access on unproved `unknown` reports error `TS2209`; strict-mode imported C# reference returns without nullable metadata report warning `TS2404` and do not block builds by themselves. Implemented imported C# nullable receiver/member/indexer/null-conditional slices lower through C# 7.3-compatible guards or report deterministic diagnostics before backend emission. Broader TypeSharp-owned nullable receiver lifting, null-conditional chains, invocation, events, local-binding assignment, and fuller legacy-nullability propagation remain post-1.0. Existing tests cover unknown C# nullability warnings, nullability build-stop diagnostics, public-boundary `unknown` rejection, unknown access diagnostics, nullable extension-property receiver diagnostics, and nullable imported member/indexer/null-conditional target failures. Docs contract assertions preserve the boundary. | Reopen only if imported C# unknown nullability becomes build-blocking, public `unknown` is promoted, TypeSharp-owned nullable receiver lifting or broader null-conditional forms are promoted, or the warning/error split changes. |
| Broad `TS2201` reduction | Done | Twenty-one high-frequency user-facing splits are implemented in the working tree: TypeSharp-authored class/interface member subset violations use `TS2210`, unsupported executable match-pattern forms use `TS2211`, advanced type-operator budget failures use `TS2212`, unsupported extension-property policy failures use `TS2213`, unsupported enum/bitwise/shift algebra failures use `TS2214`, TypeSharp-owned function application/pipeline/composition failures use `TS2215`, unsupported assignment target policy failures use `TS2216`, unsupported imported C# operator policy failures use `TS2217`, invalid match guard predicates use `TS2218`, unsupported collection/record construction expressions use `TS2219`, structural proof failures use `TS2220`, unsupported extension-method receiver shapes use `TS2221`, primitive arithmetic compound-assignment failures use `TS2222`, unsupported null-conditional read shapes use `TS2223`, invalid yield expressions use `TS2224`, invalid lock expressions use `TS2225`, invalid nominal-union match case names use `TS2226`, invalid `satisfies` expressions use `TS2227`, invalid function return expressions use `TS2228`, invalid value initializers use `TS2229`, and invalid assignment values use `TS2230` instead of broad `TS2201`. Current checker dispatch has no remaining `TS2201` emission path; the descriptor remains in the registry for compatibility and synthetic LSP mapper coverage. Docs contract assertions keep the descriptor table entries and registry wording present, and diagnostic fixture polarity now rejects stale fixture README `TS2201` wording when the expected diagnostics have moved to narrower codes. | Reopen only if a future language path reintroduces broad `TS2201` emission instead of a stable narrow descriptor. |
| TypeSharp-authored operator policy | Done | Type System, Feature Status, C# Members And Overloads, and Diagnostics now record that TypeSharp-authored operator declarations are post-1.0: records, classes, interfaces, unions, and extension declarations cannot introduce overload or conversion operators. The 1.0 operator-like surface is limited to documented built-in numeric, enum, boolean, assignment, pipeline, composition, and selected imported C# static binary metadata rules. Unsupported TypeSharp-authored nominal operands continue to report deterministic operand diagnostics before backend emission. Docs contract assertions preserve the boundary. | Reopen only if TypeSharp-authored operator syntax, overload ranking, checked/unchecked operator policy, public CLR metadata emission, or direct IL lowering is promoted into 1.0. |
| Extension member policy | Done | Type System now has a named 1.0 Extension Member Policy. TypeSharp-authored explicit-receiver extension methods lower to ordinary C# extension methods, and getter-only extension properties lower to C# 7.3-compatible `GetName(this T receiver)` helper methods. The documented boundary requires exact known non-null receiver matching for extension properties and records duplicate exact receiver/name declarations, ordinary/structural precedence conflicts, helper-name collisions, nullable receiver declarations/accesses, assignment targets, and null-conditional read/simple assignment targets as deterministic `TS2213` diagnostics before emission. Setters, static extension members, extension operators, nullable receiver lifting, imported C# extension property metadata, richer conversion/ranking, and C# 14 `extension(...)` block emission are post-1.0. Existing generated `net48` C# consumer smokes cover extension method and extension property lowering, and docs contract assertions preserve the boundary. | Reopen only if setters, static extension members, extension operators, nullable receiver lifting, imported extension property metadata, richer ranking, or C# 14 extension-block emission are promoted into 1.0. |
| Functional language scope | Done | Type System now has a named 1.0 Functional Scope Boundary. It records the accepted functional ergonomics: immutable values, expression-oriented direct `fun` declarations, explicit function types lowering to CLR delegates, nominal unions, `Option<T>`/`Result<T,E>` Core types, pattern matching inside the documented 1.0 match boundary, direct first-argument pipeline calls, unary named-function composition, lambdas in supported delegate contexts, iterator `yield`, and `Task`-based async. Reference and Type System now explicitly keep F#-complete higher-order inference, automatic currying, general partial application, imported pipeline/composition inference, pipeline overload ranking, computation expressions, active patterns, units of measure, and type providers post-1.0. Existing pipeline and composition generated `net48` C# consumer smokes cover the accepted lowering paths, and docs contract assertions preserve the boundary. | Reopen only if higher-order inference, currying, partial application, imported pipeline/composition inference, computation expressions, active patterns, units of measure, or type providers are promoted into 1.0. |
| Enum and bitwise algebra scope | Done | Type System now has a named 1.0 Enum And Bitwise Algebra Boundary. It records the accepted enum surface as TypeSharp-owned CLR enum declarations with optional integral underlying types, explicit integer values, aliases to previously declared same-enum members, initializer-local composite-or expressions, declaration/member attributes as metadata, same-enum value `|`/`&`/`^`/`~`, and match exhaustiveness for TypeSharp-owned and named imported C# enum members. It records the accepted bitwise surface as primitive integral `|`/`&`/`^`/`~`/`<<`/`>>`/`>>>`, boolean `|`/`&`/`^`, local enum/integral/bool bitwise compound assignment, primitive integral shift assignment, and bounded `>>>=` for mutable locals plus supported imported field/property/indexer targets. Unsupported enum/bitwise/shift algebra failures now report `TS2214` before backend emission. Enum-valued shifts and shift assignments, flag algebra beyond same-enum value operators, flag-aware match/pattern reasoning, imported numeric enum flag reasoning, arbitrary/general computed enum values outside initializer-local composite-or, numeric pattern algebra, numeric enum patterns, and broad attribute target validation are documented post-1.0. Existing generated `net48` C# consumer smokes cover enum declarations, integral bitwise, integral shifts, logical unsigned shifts, bitwise compound assignment, enum match, and imported C# enum match. | Reopen only if enum-valued shifts, flag-aware algebra/reasoning, imported numeric enum flag reasoning, arbitrary computed enum values, numeric pattern algebra, numeric enum patterns, or broader attribute target validation are promoted into 1.0. |
| Collection and object construction boundaries | Done | Type System now has a named 1.0 Collection And Object Construction Boundary. The accepted collection surface requires a known array or `System.Collections.Generic.List<T>` target and includes empty literals, homogeneous element literals, known array/List spreads, imported C# overload arguments selected as array/List targets, imported `params` array contexts, and lambda return bodies whose delegate return type is a known array or `List<T>`. The accepted object-construction surface includes expected nominal TypeSharp record expressions and nominal record spread lowering to constructor calls in record parameter order, plus imported C# constructor calls through the metadata-backed constructor path with deterministic overload diagnostics. Dictionary/set literals, collection-expression constructor or factory arguments beyond the documented array/List and imported overload slices, object initializer syntax, arbitrary class object construction, inferred anonymous object construction, contextual collection inference without a known array/List target, collection-builder protocols, and record/class/object initializer mutation are documented post-1.0. Existing generated `net48` C# consumer smokes cover collection expression lowering, record expression construction, imported collection overload matching, imported `params` array matching, delegate lambda collection returns, and imported constructor calls/diagnostics. | Reopen only if dictionary/set literals, broader contextual collection inference, collection-builder protocols, object initializers, arbitrary class construction, anonymous object construction, or initializer mutation are promoted into 1.0. |
| Runtime helper ABI | Done | `.NET Interop` records Runtime ABI `0` as the explicit pre-1.0 preview ABI rule, names the ABI-covered Core/Runtime helper surface, and defines when the ABI version must change. `runtime ABI constants are aligned` verifies compiler/runtime ABI and runtime target framework alignment. Core helper tests cover `Option<T>`, `Result<T,E>`, and `Unit`; runtime helper tests cover union metadata, pattern helper matching, equality/hash composition, and async `Task` helpers. The release-staged runtime artifact smoke proves generated assemblies and a C# `net48` consumer output directory carry the same installed Core/Runtime layout, and docs now state that the hosted release smoke repeats that runtime-backed consumer output shape against downloaded release assets after checksum and metadata verification. | Reopen only if Runtime ABI `0` is replaced with a stable 1.0 ABI or helper signatures/deployment shape change. |

- Split the eighth broad `TS2201` class of diagnostics by adding `TS2217` for unsupported imported C# operator policy failures, wiring missing, checked-only, instance-compound-only, ambiguous, nullable, and non-assignable imported static binary multiplicative operator failures to the new descriptor, updating inline checker assertions, documenting it, and verifying the focused build/test/docs path.
- Split the ninth broad `TS2201` class of diagnostics by adding `TS2218` for invalid match guard predicates, wiring known null, nullable, and non-bool guard expressions to the new descriptor, updating fixture/docs assertions, documenting it, and verifying the focused build/test/docs path.
- Split the tenth broad `TS2201` class of diagnostics by adding `TS2219` for unsupported collection/record construction expressions, wiring inconsistent collection elements, target element mismatches, non-array/List spread elements, missing or unknown record fields, record field mismatches, and non-record record spreads to the new descriptor, updating fixtures/docs assertions, documenting it, and verifying the focused build/test/docs path.
- Split the eleventh broad `TS2201` class of diagnostics by adding `TS2220` for structural proof failures, wiring structural assignment failures, missing structural members, impossible type-level-union discriminant literal checks, and structural member access failures to the new descriptor, updating fixtures/docs assertions, documenting it, and verifying the focused build/test/docs path.
- Split the twelfth broad `TS2201` class of diagnostics by adding `TS2221` for TypeSharp-authored extension-method receiver-shape failures, wiring missing receiver type, missing/unknown first receiver parameter, params receiver parameter, and receiver type mismatch checks to the new descriptor, updating fixture/docs assertions, documenting it, and verifying the focused build/test/docs path.
- Split the thirteenth broad `TS2201` class of diagnostics by adding `TS2222` for primitive arithmetic compound-assignment failures, wiring additive/multiplicative primitive operand and assign-back failures to the new descriptor while leaving imported operator policy on `TS2217` and target policy on `TS2216`, updating fixtures/docs assertions, documenting it, and verifying the focused build/test/docs path.
- Split the fourteenth broad `TS2201` class of diagnostics by adding `TS2223` for unsupported null-conditional read shapes, wiring unsupported `?.` member and `?[]` indexer read fallbacks to the new descriptor while leaving null-conditional assignment target policy on `TS2216` and extension-property policy on `TS2213`, updating inline/docs assertions, documenting it, and verifying the focused build/test/docs path.
- Split the fifteenth and sixteenth broad `TS2201` classes of diagnostics by adding `TS2224` for invalid iterator `yield` expressions and `TS2225` for invalid `lock` gate expressions, wiring iterator return/element failures and known non-lockable gate failures to the new descriptors while leaving yield nullability on `TS2202` and structural yield proof failures on `TS2220`, updating fixtures/docs assertions, adding non-iterator yield fixture coverage, and verifying the focused build/test/docs path.
- Split the seventeenth broad `TS2201` class of diagnostics by adding `TS2226` for invalid nominal-union match case-name patterns, wiring missing union case-name failures to the new descriptor while leaving unsupported pattern shapes on `TS2211`, invalid guards on `TS2218`, and missing coverage on `TS2203`, updating docs assertions, adding fixture coverage, and verifying the focused build/test/docs path.
- Split the eighteenth broad `TS2201` class of diagnostics by adding `TS2227` for invalid `satisfies` expressions, wiring ordinary non-nullability and non-structural assignability failures to the new descriptor while leaving nullability on `TS2202` and structural proof failures on `TS2220`, updating docs assertions, adding fixture coverage, and verifying the focused build/test/docs path.
- Split the nineteenth broad `TS2201` class of diagnostics by adding `TS2228` for invalid function return expressions, wiring ordinary non-nullability and non-structural return assignability failures to the new descriptor while leaving return nullability on `TS2202` and structural return proof failures on `TS2220`, updating fixture/docs assertions, and verifying the focused build/test/docs path.
- Split the twentieth broad `TS2201` class of diagnostics by adding `TS2229` for invalid value initializers, wiring ordinary non-nullability and non-structural annotated `let` initializer assignability failures to the new descriptor while leaving initializer nullability on `TS2202`, structural initializer proof failures on `TS2220`, and later simple assignments on `TS2201`, updating fixture/docs assertions, and verifying the focused build/test/docs path.
- Split the twenty-first broad `TS2201` class of diagnostics by adding `TS2230` for invalid assignment values, wiring ordinary non-nullability and non-structural simple assignment assignability failures to the new descriptor while leaving assignment target policy on `TS2216`, assignment nullability on `TS2202`, and structural assignment proof failures on `TS2220`, removing the final broad mismatch dispatcher, updating fixture/docs assertions, and verifying the focused build/test/docs path.
